\section{Subsetting}\label{subsetting}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Certain elements of a vector can be subsetted using the brackets
  \texttt{{[}{]}}
\end{itemize}

\includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/2_vector_index.png}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Subsetting can be done using one of the following indexing methods:

  \begin{itemize}
  \item
    Numeric indexing
  \item
    Logical indexing
  \item
    Character indexing (if the vector has names; not covered here)
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

\subsection{Numeric indexing}\label{numeric-indexing}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Numeric indexing means telling R the specific indices to return
  values.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#       1   2   3   4   5   6   7}
\NormalTok{v }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{66}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{82}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{85}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{78}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{90}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{73}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 1st value}
\NormalTok{v[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]            }

\CommentTok{\# 4th value}
\NormalTok{v[}\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{]            }

\CommentTok{\# last value, 7th value}
\NormalTok{v[}\FunctionTok{length}\NormalTok{(v)]    }

\CommentTok{\# Not available}
\NormalTok{v[}\DecValTok{320}\NormalTok{]          }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Numeric indexing can also use a vector of multiple indices.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# at 2nd, 3rd, 4th, 5th}
\NormalTok{v[}\DecValTok{2}\SpecialCharTok{:}\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{]                 }

\CommentTok{\# at 5th, 4th, 3rd, 2nd}
\NormalTok{v[}\DecValTok{5}\SpecialCharTok{:}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]                 }

\CommentTok{\# at 3rd, 1st, 3rd, 5th, 2nd}
\NormalTok{v[}\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{)]    }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Note that negative indices mean all but the specified indices.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# all but 1st value}
\NormalTok{v[}\SpecialCharTok{{-}}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]                    }

\CommentTok{\# all but 2nd and 5th values}
\NormalTok{v[}\SpecialCharTok{{-}}\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{5}\NormalTok{)]              }

\CommentTok{\# all but 1st to 4th values}
\NormalTok{v[}\SpecialCharTok{{-}}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{1}\SpecialCharTok{:}\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{)]                }

\CommentTok{\# error!}
\NormalTok{v[}\SpecialCharTok{{-}}\DecValTok{1}\SpecialCharTok{:}\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{]                  }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Consider the following vector

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#       1   2   3   4   5   6   7}
\NormalTok{v }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{66}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{82}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{85}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{78}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{90}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{73}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  The second value
\item
  The sixth value
\item
  The first and last values.
\item
  The values at positions 3 through 6
\item
  The values at positions 6 through 3
\item
  The values at positions 1, 4, and 7
\item
  All values except the first.
\item
  All values except the last two.
\item
  All values except positions 2 and 6.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\subsection{Logical Indexing}\label{logical-indexing}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Logical indexing} means telling R which values to return and
  which values not to return.
\item
  With logical indexing, \texttt{TRUE} will retain the elements, while
  \texttt{FALSE} will discard the elements.
\item
  Logical indexing is powerful because it allows for subsetting with
  conditions.
\item
  Consider the following vector
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#       1   2   3   4   5   6   7}
\NormalTok{v }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{66}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{82}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{85}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{78}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{90}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{73}\NormalTok{)}

\CommentTok{\# 1st, 6th}
\NormalTok{v[}\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{)]    }

\CommentTok{\# 2nd, 3rd, 4th}
\NormalTok{v[}\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{)]     }

\CommentTok{\# those values greater than 80}
\NormalTok{v[v }\SpecialCharTok{\textgreater{}} \DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{]    }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Consider the following vector

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#       1   2   3   4   5   6   7}
\NormalTok{v }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{66}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{82}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{85}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{78}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{90}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{73}\NormalTok{)}

\begin{itemize}

\item

\item
  At least \(\$15\)
\item
  To be the smallest
\item
  To be the largest
\end{itemize}

\section{Useful functions for
vectors}\label{useful-functions-for-vectors}

Given a vector,

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{head()} returns its first few elements
\item
  \texttt{tail()} returns its last few elements
\item
  \texttt{sort()} returns its sorted version in increasing or decreasing
  order
\item
  \texttt{order()} returns the indices of its sorted version
\item
  \texttt{rev()} returns the reversed vector
\item
  \texttt{unique()} returns a vector of its unique elements
\item
  \texttt{table()} shows unique elements and their frequencies
\end{itemize}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

The monthly cost for a stand-alone drug plan varies from plan to plan
and from state to state. The vector \texttt{cost} gives the premium for
the plan with the lowest cost for each state in 2005 (excludes District
of Columbia).

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{cost }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}
  \FloatTok{14.08}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{20.05}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.14}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.31}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{5.41}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{8.62}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{7.32}\NormalTok{,}
  \FloatTok{6.44}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.35}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{17.91}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{17.18}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.33}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{13.32}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{12.30}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}\NormalTok{,}
  \FloatTok{9.48}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{12.30}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{17.06}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{19.60}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.44}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{7.32}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{13.75}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}\NormalTok{,}
  \FloatTok{11.60}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.29}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.42}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{19.60}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{4.43}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.65}\NormalTok{,}
  \FloatTok{4.10}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{13.27}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{14.43}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.07}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.93}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.14}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{7.32}\NormalTok{,}
  \FloatTok{16.57}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{14.08}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{10.31}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.33}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{7.32}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{8.81}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{6.93}\NormalTok{,}
  \FloatTok{10.14}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{11.42}\NormalTok{, }\FloatTok{1.87}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Try the following R code and see what it returns.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{head}\NormalTok{(cost)    }\CommentTok{\# head(cost, n = 6)}

\FunctionTok{tail}\NormalTok{(cost)    }\CommentTok{\# tail(cost, n = 6)}

\FunctionTok{sort}\NormalTok{(cost)}

\chapter{2C: Character Vector and
Factor}\label{c-character-vector-and-factor}

\section{Readings}\label{readings-2}

From \textbf{R Coding Basics: An Introduction to the Basics of Coding in
R} by Dr.~Gaston Sanchez:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \href{https://www.gastonsanchez.com/R-coding-basics/2-01-factors.html}{Factors}
\end{itemize}

\section{Topics}\label{topics-3}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Character vector
\item
  Useful functions for character vector
\item
  Factor
\end{itemize}

\section{Character vector}\label{character-vector}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Data can be in the form of specific categories that describe a certain
  characteristic.
\item
  Categories such as gender, color, nationality, and college major are
  said to be \textbf{nominal} because they have \ul{no} natural
  ordering.
\item
  In contrast, categories such as education level, customer
  satisfaction, and Likert scale responses, are \textbf{ordinal} because
  they do have a natural ordering.
\item
  In R, a \textbf{character vector} is often used to represent nominal
  categories.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# character vector}
\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)  }
\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Math\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Data Science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Math\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Computer Science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Data Science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)  }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{Useful functions for character
vector}\label{useful-functions-for-character-vector}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{The \texttt{nchar()}
function}{The nchar() function}}\label{the-nchar-function}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{nchar()} counts the number of characters of each element.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{v }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Data\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}science\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}is\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}fun\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}and\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}challenging\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\FunctionTok{nchar}\NormalTok{(v)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1]  4  7  2  3  3 11
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{strsplit()} splits a string into words.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{strsplit}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Data science is fun and challenging\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{split =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{} \textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[[1]]
[1] "Data"        "science"     "is"          "fun"         "and"        
[6] "challenging"
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{paste()} concatenates elements of character vectors
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{towns }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Glassboro\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Clayton\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Pitman\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Deptford\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{paste}\NormalTok{(towns, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}NJ\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Glassboro NJ" "Clayton NJ"   "Pitman NJ"    "Deptford NJ" 
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{paste}\NormalTok{(towns, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}NJ\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{} \textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Glassboro NJ" "Clayton NJ"   "Pitman NJ"    "Deptford NJ" 
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{paste}\NormalTok{(towns, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}NJ\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}, \textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Glassboro, NJ" "Clayton, NJ"   "Pitman, NJ"    "Deptford, NJ" 
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Glassboro in NJ" "Clayton in NJ"   "Pitman in NJ"    "Deptford in NJ" 
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Thanks to vectorization, \texttt{paste()} allows corresponding
  elements to be concatenated.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{first\_names }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}James\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Robert\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Mary\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{last\_names  }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Smith\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Williams\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Brown\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{paste}\NormalTok{(first\_names, last\_names)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "James Smith"     "Robert Williams" "Mary Brown"     
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{zip\_code }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}08028\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}08312\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}08071\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}08096\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{paste0}\NormalTok{(towns, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}, NJ \textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, zip\_code)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Glassboro, NJ 08028" "Clayton, NJ 08312"   "Pitman, NJ 08071"   
[4] "Deptford, NJ 08096" 
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Factor}\label{factor}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  A \textbf{factor} is a specialized data structure for categories,
  especially ordinal categories.
\item
  It behaves like a vector but has additional attributes.
\item
  A factor displays categories (levels) but stores them internally as
  integers.
\item
  A factor is created from a character vector using the
  \texttt{factor()} function.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\DocumentationTok{\#\#\# Nominal factor}

\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} [1] O  A  AB O  O  B  A  B  AB}
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} Levels: A B AB O}

\DocumentationTok{\#\#\# Ordinal factor}

\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{}  [1] extra hot mild      hot       mild      medium    extra hot mild     }
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{}  [8] medium    extra hot medium    extra hot mild     }
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} Levels: mild \textless{} medium \textless{} hot \textless{} extra hot}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Create a nominal factor from the following character vector:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{blood }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}O\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}AB\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}O\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}O\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}AB\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{factor}\NormalTok{(blood, }\AttributeTok{levels =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}O\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}A\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}B\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}AB\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] O  A  AB O  O  B  A  B  AB
Levels: O A B AB
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Create an ordinal factor from the following character vector:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{pepper }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}extra hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mild\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mild\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}medium\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}extra hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }
            \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mild\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}medium\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}extra hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}medium\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}extra hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mild\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{factor}\NormalTok{(pepper, }\AttributeTok{levels =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mild\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}medium\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}extra hot\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{), }\AttributeTok{ordered =} \ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
 [1] extra hot mild      hot       mild      medium    extra hot mild     
 [8] medium    extra hot medium    extra hot mild     
Levels: mild < medium < hot < extra hot
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\end{Highlighting}

       \AttributeTok{labels =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Small\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Medium\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Large\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Extra Large\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}

\chapter{3A: Data Frame}\label{a-data-frame}

\section{Readings}\label{readings-3}

From \textbf{R Coding Basics: An Introduction to the Basics of Coding in
R} by Dr.~Gaston Sanchez:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \href{https://www.gastonsanchez.com/R-coding-basics/4-02-data-frames.html}{Data
  Frames}
\end{itemize}

\section{Topics}\label{topics-4}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Data frame and matrix
\item
  Creating a data frame
\item
  Selecting elements in a data frame
\item
  Adding, removing, and transforming a column
\end{itemize}

\section{Data Frame}\label{data-frame}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  A \textbf{matrix} is a tabular data structure containing values of the
  \ul{same} type.
\item
  A \textbf{data frame} is a matrix-like data structure in which each
  column may have a \ul{different} type.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#   Age Height Weight Gender}
\CommentTok{\# 1  25    168     65 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 2  32    175     70   Male}
\CommentTok{\# 3  28    160     55 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 4  40    180     80   Male}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  To create a data frame, we can combine multiple vectors using
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{age }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{25}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{28}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{hei }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{168}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{175}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{wei }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{gen }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{"Female"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Male"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Female"}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{"Male"}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{data.frame}\NormalTok{(age, hei, wei, gen)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  age hei wei    gen
1  25 168  65 Female
2  32 175  70   Male
3  28 160  55 Female
4  40 180  80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  It is possible to specify the column names.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{age }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{25}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{28}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{hei }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{168}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{175}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{wei }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{gen }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{data.frame}\NormalTok{(}\AttributeTok{Age =}\NormalTok{ age, }\AttributeTok{Height =}\NormalTok{ hei, }\AttributeTok{Weight =}\NormalTok{ wei, }\AttributeTok{Gender =}\NormalTok{ gen)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
1  25    168     65 Female
2  32    175     70   Male
3  28    160     55 Female
4  40    180     80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  We can also type in the values directly.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{data.frame}\NormalTok{(}
  \AttributeTok{Age    =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{25}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{28}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Height =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{168}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{175}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Weight =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Gender =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
1  25    168     65 Female
2  32    175     70   Male
3  28    160     55 Female
4  40    180     80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\section{Subsetting}\label{subsetting-1}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{The dollar operator
\texttt{\$}}{The dollar operator \$}}\label{the-dollar-operator}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  A specific column (variable) can be quickly accessed using the dollar
  operator \texttt{\$}
\item
  Note that the output is a vector, not a data frame.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{data.frame}\NormalTok{(}
  \AttributeTok{Age    =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{25}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{28}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Height =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{168}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{175}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Weight =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Gender =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Height}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 168 175 160 180
\end{verbatim}

\subsection{\texorpdfstring{The brackets
\texttt{{[}{]}}}{The brackets {[}{]}}}\label{the-brackets}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Certain elements of a data frame can be subset using the brackets
  \texttt{{[}{]}}
\end{itemize}

\begin{figure}[H]

{\centering \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/3_dat_index.png}

}

\caption{From Dr.~Gaston Sanchez}

\end{figure}%

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Write R code to subset the indicated values of \texttt{df}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#   Age Height Weight Gender}
\CommentTok{\# 1  25    168     65 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 2  32    175     70   Male}
\CommentTok{\# 3  28    160     55 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 4  40    180     80   Male}

\CommentTok{\# row 1, column 3}

\CommentTok{\# row 4, column 4}

\CommentTok{\# row 3, column 2}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# row 1, column 3}
\NormalTok{df[}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 65
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# row 4, column 4}
\NormalTok{df[}\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Male"
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# row 3, column 2}
\NormalTok{df[}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 160
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{Subsetting rows}\label{subsetting-rows}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Subsetting rows can be done using numeric indexing with the brackets
  \texttt{{[}{]}}
\end{itemize}

\begin{figure}[H]

{\centering \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/3_dat_rows.png}

}

\caption{From Dr.~Gaston Sanchez}

\end{figure}%

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Write R code to subset the indicated values of \texttt{df}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#   Age Height Weight Gender}
\CommentTok{\# 1  25    168     65 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 2  32    175     70   Male}
\CommentTok{\# 3  28    160     55 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 4  40    180     80   Male}

\CommentTok{\# row 3}

\CommentTok{\# rows 2 to 4 (2, 3, 4)}

\CommentTok{\# rows 1, 2, and 4 only}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# row 3}
\NormalTok{df[}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, ]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
3  28    160     55 Female
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# rows 2 to 4 (2, 3, 4)}
\NormalTok{df[}\DecValTok{2}\SpecialCharTok{:}\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{, ]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
2  32    175     70   Male
3  28    160     55 Female
4  40    180     80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# rows 1, 2, and 4 only}
\NormalTok{df[}\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{), ]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
1  25    168     65 Female
2  32    175     70   Male
4  40    180     80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Try the following R code to see what it returns.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\NormalTok{df[df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Gender }\SpecialCharTok{==} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, ]}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{Shaded}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender

4  40    180     80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
1  25    168     65 Female
3  28    160     55 Female
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df[df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Age }\SpecialCharTok{\textless{}} \DecValTok{30}\NormalTok{, ]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
1  25    168     65 Female
3  28    160     55 Female
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\subsection{Subsetting columns}\label{subsetting-columns}

\begin{figure}[H]

{\centering \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/3_dat_cols.png}

}

\caption{From Dr.~Gaston Sanchez}

\end{figure}%

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Write R code to subset the indicated values of \texttt{df}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#   Age Height Weight Gender}
\CommentTok{\# 1  25    168     65 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 2  32    175     70   Male}
\CommentTok{\# 3  28    160     55 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 4  40    180     80   Male}

\CommentTok{\# column 1}

\CommentTok{\# columns 1 to 3 (1, 2, 3)}

\CommentTok{\# columns 1, 3, and 4 only}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# column 1}
\NormalTok{df[, }\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 25 32 28 40
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# columns 1 to 3 (1, 2, 3)}
\NormalTok{df[, }\DecValTok{1}\SpecialCharTok{:}\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight
1  25    168     65
2  32    175     70
3  28    160     55
4  40    180     80
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# columns 1, 3, and 4 only}
\NormalTok{df[}\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{3}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{4}\NormalTok{), ]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender
1  25    168     65 Female
3  28    160     55 Female
4  40    180     80   Male
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Another way to subset column(s) of a data frame is to use the brackets
  \texttt{{[}{]}} with column name(s). If more than one column name are
  given, the output is a data frame.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df[, }\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Age\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Gender\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Gender
1  25 Female
2  32   Male
3  28 Female
4  40   Male
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Otherwise, the ouput is a vector.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df[, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Height\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 168 175 160 180
\end{verbatim}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Write R code to subset the indicated column(s) of \texttt{df} using the
brackets \texttt{{[}{]}}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#   Age Height Weight Gender}
\CommentTok{\# 1  25    168     65 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 2  32    175     70   Male}
\CommentTok{\# 3  28    160     55 Female}
\CommentTok{\# 4  40    180     80   Male}

\CommentTok{\# Height, Weight}

\CommentTok{\# Gender, Weight, Age}

\CommentTok{\# Gender}

\CommentTok{\# Age}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Height, Weight}
\NormalTok{df[, }\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Height\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Weight\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Height Weight
1    168     65
2    175     70
3    160     55
4    180     80
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Gender, Weight, Age}
\NormalTok{df[, }\FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Gender\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Weight\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Age\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Gender Weight Age
1 Female     65  25
2   Male     70  32
3 Female     55  28
4   Male     80  40
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Gender}
\NormalTok{df[, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Gender\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] "Female" "Male"   "Female" "Male"  
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Age}
\NormalTok{df[, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Age\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{]}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
[1] 25 32 28 40
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Adding a column}\label{adding-a-column}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Using the dollar operator \texttt{\$} is the easiest way to add a
  column
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{data.frame}\NormalTok{(}
  \AttributeTok{Age    =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{25}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{32}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{28}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{40}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Height =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{168}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{175}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{160}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{180}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Weight =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{65}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{70}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{55}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{80}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{Gender =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Female\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Male\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)}

\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Home }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Pitman\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Glassboro\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Clayton\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Deptford\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{df}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender      Home
1  25    168     65 Female    Pitman
2  32    175     70   Male Glassboro
3  28    160     55 Female   Clayton
4  40    180     80   Male  Deptford
\end{verbatim}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Create a new data frame as follows:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{}   Age Height Weight Gender      Home Married Savings}
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} 1  25    168     65 Female    Pitman    TRUE   10000}
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} 2  32    175     70   Male Glassboro    TRUE   25000}
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} 3  28    160     55 Female   Clayton   FALSE    7000}
\CommentTok{\#\textgreater{} 4  40    180     80   Male  Deptford    TRUE   40000}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Married }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{FALSE}\NormalTok{, }\ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Savings }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{10000}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{25000}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{7000}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{40000}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{df}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender      Home Married Savings
1  25    168     65 Female    Pitman    TRUE   10000
2  32    175     70   Male Glassboro    TRUE   25000
3  28    160     55 Female   Clayton   FALSE    7000
4  40    180     80   Male  Deptford    TRUE   40000
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Removing a column}\label{removing-a-column}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Removing a column can be done with the dollar operator \texttt{\$} as
  follows:
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Home }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \ConstantTok{NULL}
\NormalTok{df}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender Married Savings
1  25    168     65 Female    TRUE   10000
2  32    175     70   Male    TRUE   25000
3  28    160     55 Female   FALSE    7000
4  40    180     80   Male    TRUE   40000
\end{verbatim}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Remove the column \texttt{Married} in \texttt{df}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Married }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \ConstantTok{NULL}
\NormalTok{df}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender Savings
1  25    168     65 Female   10000
2  32    175     70   Male   25000
3  28    160     55 Female    7000
4  40    180     80   Male   40000
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Transforming a column}\label{transforming-a-column}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The dollar operator \texttt{\$} allows us to subset and transform a
  column.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Savings }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}}\NormalTok{ df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Savings }\SpecialCharTok{/} \DecValTok{1000}
\NormalTok{df}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height Weight Gender Savings
1  25    168     65 Female      10
2  32    175     70   Male      25
3  28    160     55 Female       7
4  40    180     80   Male      40
\end{verbatim}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Convert \texttt{Weight} in kilograms to lbs

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Weight }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}}\NormalTok{ df}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{Weight }\SpecialCharTok{*} \FloatTok{2.20462}
\NormalTok{df}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Age Height   Weight Gender Savings
1  25    168 143.3003 Female      10
2  32    175 154.3234   Male      25
3  28    160 121.2541 Female       7
4  40    180 176.3696   Male      40
\end{verbatim}

\end{tcolorbox}

\chapter{3B: Importing Data Frame}\label{b-importing-data-frame}

\section{Readings}\label{readings-4}

From \textbf{R Coding Basics: An Introduction to the Basics of Coding in
R} by Dr.~Gaston Sanchez:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \href{https://www.gastonsanchez.com/R-coding-basics/6-02-import-tables.html}{Import
  Data Tables}
\end{itemize}

\section{Topics}\label{topics-5}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Built-in data sets
\item
  Importing data
\item
  Inspecting a data frame
\item
  Storing data and objects
\end{itemize}

\section{Built-in data frames}\label{built-in-data-frames}

R has many built-in data sets:

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{faithful} Old Faithful Geyser Data
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{head}\NormalTok{(faithful)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  eruptions waiting
1     3.600      79
2     1.800      54
3     3.333      74
4     2.283      62
5     4.533      85
6     2.883      55
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{iris} Edgar Anderson's Iris Data
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{head}\NormalTok{(iris)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
  Sepal.Length Sepal.Width Petal.Length Petal.Width Species
1          5.1         3.5          1.4         0.2  setosa
2          4.9         3.0          1.4         0.2  setosa
3          4.7         3.2          1.3         0.2  setosa
4          4.6         3.1          1.5         0.2  setosa
5          5.0         3.6          1.4         0.2  setosa
6          5.4         3.9          1.7         0.4  setosa
\end{verbatim}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \texttt{mtcars} Motor Trend Car Road Tests
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}

\section{Reading data from the
clipboard}\label{reading-data-from-the-clipboard}

A data frame can be made by reading from the clipboard as follows:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Select and copy the content from a data file

  \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/3_loan50.png}
\item
  Use the \texttt{read.delim()} function
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{read.delim}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}clipboard\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{\texorpdfstring{Importing data with \texttt{read.table()} and
\texttt{read.csv()}}{Importing data with read.table() and read.csv()}}\label{importing-data-with-read.table-and-read.csv}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Small and medium-size data sets are usually stored in a \textbf{text
  file} \texttt{.txt}
\item
  Data in a text file are separated by a \textbf{delimiter} such as
  white space, comma, tab, or semi-colon.
\item
  A text file in which data are separated by a comma is equivalent to a
  \textbf{comma-separated value} file \texttt{.csv}, which is commonly
  used in statistics and data science due to portability.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\DocumentationTok{\#\#\# comma{-}separated value}

\NormalTok{floor,bed,lease,pool,rent}
\NormalTok{first,}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{9}\NormalTok{,yes,}\DecValTok{1200}
\NormalTok{second,}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{,no,}\DecValTok{1550}
\NormalTok{first,}\DecValTok{2}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{,yes,}\DecValTok{1900}
\NormalTok{second,}\DecValTok{1}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{9}\NormalTok{,no,}\DecValTok{1650}
\NormalTok{first,}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{,}\DecValTok{12}\NormalTok{,yes,}\DecValTok{1300}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{read.table()} function is a general function to read data
  from a text file. Before using the function, it is best to move the
  text file under the current working directory.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{header =} \ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{} \textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{header =} \ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{},\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{header =} \ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}}\SpecialCharTok{\textbackslash{}t}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{header =} \ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{};\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{read.csv()} function is just a wrapper of the
  \texttt{read.table()} function for importing comma-separated value
  file \texttt{.csv}
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{read.csv}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)    }\CommentTok{\# same as read.table(\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}, sep = \textquotesingle{},\textquotesingle{})}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Import the \texttt{apartment} data.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

The below code assumes that we have \texttt{apartment.txt} and
\texttt{apartment.csv} in our current working directory. To identify our
current working directory, type in the console \texttt{getwd()}.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{read.table}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}apartment.txt\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{header =} \ConstantTok{TRUE}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{};\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Inspecting a data frame}\label{inspecting-a-data-frame}

Given a data frame,

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{str()} shows its overall structure
\item
  \texttt{head()} returns its first few rows
\item
  \texttt{tail()} returns its last few rows
\item
  \texttt{dim()} returns a vector dimensions
\item
  \texttt{nrow()} returns its number of rows
\item
  \texttt{ncol()} returns its number of columns
\item
  \texttt{colnames()} and \texttt{names()} returns its column names
\item
  \texttt{rownames()} returns its row names
\item
  \texttt{summary()} shows descriptive statistics for its columns
\item
  \texttt{complete.cases()} returns a logical vector indicating which
  observations have no missing values.
\end{itemize}

Inspect the \texttt{iris} data.

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Import and inspect the \texttt{loan50} data from
\href{https://www.openintro.org/data/index.php?data=loan50}{OpenIntro}.

\begin{quote}
This data set represents 50 loans made through the Lending Club
platform, which is a platform that allows individuals to lend to other
individuals. Of course, not all loans are created equal. Someone who is
a essentially a sure bet to pay back a loan will have an easier time
getting a loan with a low interest rate than someone who appears to be
riskier. And for people who are very risky? They may not even get a loan
offer, or they may not have accepted the loan offer due to a high
interest rate.
\end{quote}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{state} - Two-letter state code.
\item
  \texttt{emp\_length} - Number of years in the job, rounded down. If
  longer than 10 years, then this is represented by the value 10.
\item
  \texttt{term} - The number of months of the loan the applicant
  received.
\item
  \texttt{home\_ownership} - The ownership status of the applicant's
  residence.
\item
  \texttt{annual\_income} - Annual income.
\item
  \texttt{verified\_income} - Type of verification of the applicant's
  income.
\item
  \texttt{debt\_to\_income} - Debt-to-income ratio.
\item
  \texttt{total\_credit\_limit} - Total available credit, e.g.~if only
  credit cards, then the total of all the credit limits. This excludes a
  mortgage.
\item
  \texttt{total\_credit\_utilized} - Total credit balance, excluding a
  mortgage.
\item
  \texttt{num\_cc\_carrying\_balance} - Number of credit cards that are
  carrying a balance.
\item
  \texttt{loan\_amount} - The amount of the loan the applicant received.
\item
  \texttt{grade} - Grade associated with the loan.
\item
  \texttt{interest\_rate} - Interest rate of the loan the applicant
  received.
\item
  \texttt{public\_record\_bankrupt} - Number of bankruptcies listed in
  the public record for this applicant.
\item
  \texttt{loan\_status} - Status of the loan.
\item
  \texttt{has\_second\_income} - Whether the applicant has a secondary
  income.
\item
  \texttt{total\_income} - The applicant's total income.
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

If we have \texttt{loan50.csv} in our current working directory, we can
also use
\texttt{read.csv(\textquotesingle{}loan50.csv\textquotesingle{})}.
Otherwise, we can read the data set as follows:

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{loan }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{read.csv}\NormalTok{(}\FunctionTok{url}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}https://raw.githubusercontent.com/hungtong/DS{-}01{-}101/refs/heads/main/dataset/loan50.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

Once we have the data set in R, we can inspect the data as below.

\FunctionTok{rownames}\NormalTok{(loan)}
\end{Highlighting}

\section{\texorpdfstring{Storing data with \texttt{write.table()} and
\texttt{write.csv()}}{Storing data with write.table() and write.csv()}}\label{storing-data-with-write.table-and-write.csv}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  To export a data frame to \texttt{.txt} or \texttt{.csv} files, we can
  use the \texttt{write.table()} and \texttt{write.csv()} functions with
  different delimiters.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{write.table}\NormalTok{(data\_to\_store, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.txt\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{write.table}\NormalTok{(data\_to\_store, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.txt\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}}\SpecialCharTok{\textbackslash{}t}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{write.csv}\NormalTok{(data\_to\_store, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Export loans that are fully paid from the \texttt{loan50} data to
\texttt{.txt} or \texttt{.csv} files.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

One example to save the fully paid loans is

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{loan\_paid }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}}\NormalTok{ loan[loan}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{loan\_status }\SpecialCharTok{==} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Fully Paid\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, ]}

\FunctionTok{write.table}\NormalTok{(loan\_paid, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}fully\_paid\_loan.txt\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\AttributeTok{sep =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{},\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}

\FunctionTok{write.csv}\NormalTok{(loan\_paid, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}fully\_paid\_loan.csv\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{\texorpdfstring{Storing objects with
\texttt{dput()}}{Storing objects with dput()}}\label{storing-objects-with-dput}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{dput()} function writes an R object in a plain-text format
  that can be used to reproduce the object.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{dput}\NormalTok{(some\_object)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Write loans that are fully paid from the \texttt{loan50} data in a
plain-text format.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

The output can be ugly but running it in the console will reproduce the
object.

\section{\texorpdfstring{Storing objects with
\texttt{save()}}{Storing objects with save()}}\label{storing-objects-with-save}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  The \texttt{save()} allows us to store multiple objects in
  \texttt{.rdata} or \texttt{.rda}.
\end{itemize}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{save}\NormalTok{(object1, object2, object3, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}file\_name.rdata\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Identify the following objects from the \texttt{loan50} data and store
them in \texttt{.rdata}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{loan\_mortgage} - loans associated with homeownership that is
  mortgage
\item
  \texttt{loan\_20k} - loans with the loan amount at least \(20,000\)
\item
  \texttt{loan\_low\_interest} - loans with interest rate less than
  \(7\%\)
\end{itemize}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

If we run the following code, a \texttt{special\_loans.rdata} file will
be created in the current working directory. If we share this file with
someone else and they double-click it, the three saved objects
\texttt{loan\_mortgage}, \texttt{loan\_20k}, and
\texttt{loan\_low\_interest} will be made ready on their end.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{loan\_mortgage }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}}\NormalTok{ loan[loan}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{homeownership }\SpecialCharTok{==} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}mortage\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, ]}

\NormalTok{loan\_20k }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}}\NormalTok{ loan[loan}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{loan\_amount }\SpecialCharTok{\textgreater{}=} \DecValTok{20000}\NormalTok{, ]}

\NormalTok{loan\_low\_interest }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}}\NormalTok{ loan[loan}\SpecialCharTok{$}\NormalTok{interest\_rate }\SpecialCharTok{\textless{}} \DecValTok{7}\NormalTok{, ]}

\FunctionTok{save}\NormalTok{(loan\_mortgage, loan\_20k, loan\_low\_interest, }\AttributeTok{file =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}special\_loans.rdata\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Miscellaneous functions}\label{miscellaneous-functions}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{ls()} shows all the created objects
\item
  \texttt{rm()} removes certain objects
\item
  \texttt{getwd()} returns the file path of the current working
  directory
\item
  \texttt{setwd()} sets a new working directory
\end{itemize}

\chapter{4A: Examining Categorical
Variables}\label{a-examining-categorical-variables}

\section{Data Sets}\label{data-sets}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{load}\NormalTok{(}\FunctionTok{url}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}https://github.com/hungtong/DS{-}01{-}101/raw/refs/heads/main/dataset/l4a\_data.rdata\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}
\FunctionTok{load}\NormalTok{(}\FunctionTok{url}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}https://github.com/hungtong/DS{-}01{-}101/raw/refs/heads/main/dataset/cdc.rdata\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{Topics}\label{topics-6}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Basic variable types
\item
  Frequency distribution, mode, and bar plot
\item
  Stacked and side-by-side bar plot
\end{itemize}

\section{Basic variable types}\label{basic-variable-types}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Data are commonly organized into a \textbf{data matrix}. In this
  format, each row is an \textbf{observation} and each column is a
  \textbf{variable} or \textbf{feature}.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=5.44792in,height=\textheight]{index_files/mediabag/4_matr.png}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Roughly speaking, a variable can be \textbf{numerical} or
  \textbf{categorical}.
\end{itemize}

\includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/4_var_type.png}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  A \textbf{numerical variable} represents numbers that are meaningful
  to add, subtract, or take averages.
\item
  A \textbf{categorical variable} refers to specific categories that
  describe a characteristic.
\end{itemize}

\section{Examining a categorical
variable}\label{examining-a-categorical-variable}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  A \textbf{frequency distribution} is a tabular summary of data showing
  the number (frequency) of observations in each categories.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=2.875in,height=\textheight]{index_files/mediabag/4_freq.png}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  The \textbf{mode} is the category that appears the most. There can be
  multiple modes.
\item
  A \textbf{bar plot} visualizes the frequency distribution of a
  categorical variable using bars of different heights.
\end{itemize}

\section{Examining two categorical
variables}\label{examining-two-categorical-variables}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  A \textbf{contingency table} is a tabular summary of data for two
  categorical variables showing the frequency of their shared
  characteristics.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=4.98958in,height=\textheight]{index_files/mediabag/4_twoway.png}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Stacked bar plot} can be used to visualize the contingency
  table.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=4.625in,height=\textheight]{index_files/mediabag/4_stacked.png}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  \textbf{Side-by-side bar plot} is also a good option.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics[width=4.28125in,height=\textheight]{index_files/mediabag/4_side_bar.png}
\end{center}

\section{Obtaining frequency distribution and bar plot in
R}\label{obtaining-frequency-distribution-and-bar-plot-in-r}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Frequency distribution for a categorical variable can be obtained
  using the \texttt{table()} function.
\item
  Bar plot can be generated using the \texttt{barplot()} function.
  Horizontal or vertical bars can be made by adjusting
  \texttt{horiz\ =\ TRUE}.
\item
  Common graphical parameters in base R plotting include:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \texttt{col} - add color to the plot
  \item
    \texttt{main} - main title label
  \item
    \texttt{xlab} - label for x-axis
  \item
    \texttt{ylab} - label for y-axis
  \item
    \texttt{xlim} - x-axis range
  \item
    \texttt{ylim} - y-axis range
  \item
    \texttt{cex.main} - size of main title
  \item
    \texttt{cex.lab} - size of axis labels
  \item
    \texttt{cex.axis} - size of tick labels
  \end{itemize}
\item
  For predefined and hex-value colors, check out the following websites:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \href{https://r-charts.com/colors/}{R Charts}
  \item
    \href{https://www.color-hex.com/}{color-hex}
  \item
    \href{https://colorbrewer2.org/\#type=sequential&scheme=BuGn&n=3}{Color
    Brewer 2.0}
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Obtain the frequency distribution and bar plot of the
\texttt{soft\_drink} data set.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

To obtain the frequency distribution and bar plot of the
\texttt{soft\_drink} data set, we use the \texttt{table()} and
\texttt{barplot()} functions.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{freq }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{table}\NormalTok{(soft\_drink)}
\NormalTok{freq}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
soft_drink
 Coca-Cola  Diet Coke Dr. Pepper      Pepsi     Sprite 
        19          8          5         13          5 
\end{verbatim}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{barplot}\NormalTok{(}
\NormalTok{  freq,}
  \AttributeTok{col       =} \StringTok{"\#FFCC00"}\NormalTok{,       }\CommentTok{\# add color}
  \AttributeTok{main      =} \StringTok{"Bar Plot"}\NormalTok{,      }\CommentTok{\# main title}
  \AttributeTok{xlab      =} \StringTok{"Soft Drink"}\NormalTok{,    }\CommentTok{\# label for x{-}axis}
  \AttributeTok{ylab      =} \StringTok{"Frequency"}\NormalTok{,     }\CommentTok{\# label for y{-}axis}
  \AttributeTok{cex.main  =} \FloatTok{1.5}\NormalTok{,             }\CommentTok{\# size of title}
  \AttributeTok{cex.lab   =} \FloatTok{1.2}\NormalTok{,             }\CommentTok{\# size of axis labels }
  \AttributeTok{cex.axis  =} \FloatTok{1.2}\NormalTok{,             }\CommentTok{\# size of tick labels}
  \AttributeTok{cex.names =} \FloatTok{1.2}\NormalTok{,             }\CommentTok{\# size of categories}
  \AttributeTok{ylim      =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{0}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{20}\NormalTok{)         }\CommentTok{\# y{-}axis range}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{ls4a_plotting_files/figure-pdf/unnamed-chunk-2-1.pdf}

\end{tcolorbox}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Try the following code and describe the difference between the two
methods of generating a bar plot for the \texttt{activity} data set.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{freq }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{table}\NormalTok{(activity)}

\CommentTok{\# Method 1}
\FunctionTok{barplot}\NormalTok{(freq)}

\CommentTok{\# Method 2}
\FunctionTok{barplot}\NormalTok{(}
  \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{2183}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{757}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1520}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{names.arg =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sedentary\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Active\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Very Active\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)  }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

Note the frequency distribution of the \texttt{activity} data set.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\NormalTok{freq }\OtherTok{\textless{}{-}} \FunctionTok{table}\NormalTok{(activity)}
\NormalTok{freq}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\begin{verbatim}
activity
     Active   Sedentary Very Active 
        757        2183        1520 
\end{verbatim}

Using method 1, we obtain

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Method 1}
\FunctionTok{barplot}\NormalTok{(freq)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{ls4a_plotting_files/figure-pdf/unnamed-chunk-5-1.pdf}

By default, \texttt{table()} and \texttt{barplot()} will arrange
categories in the alphabetical order, which is not necessarily the
natural order of ordinal categories. For ordinal categories, it is
better than to manually rearrange the categories as in method 2.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\CommentTok{\# Method 2}
\FunctionTok{barplot}\NormalTok{(}
  \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\DecValTok{2183}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{757}\NormalTok{, }\DecValTok{1520}\NormalTok{), }
  \AttributeTok{names.arg =} \FunctionTok{c}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Sedentary\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Active\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{, }\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Very Active\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{)}
\NormalTok{)  }
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{ls4a_plotting_files/figure-pdf/unnamed-chunk-6-1.pdf}

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Stacked and side-by-side bar plot in
R}\label{stacked-and-side-by-side-bar-plot-in-r}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  For two categorical variables, the \texttt{table()} function produces
  a contingency table.
\item
  By default, stacked bar plot will be made. However, side-by-side bar
  plot can be made by setting \texttt{beside\ =\ TRUE}.
\item
  Setting \texttt{legend\ =\ TRUE} and giving a vector of colors to
  \texttt{col} will help differentiate the categories.
\end{itemize}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Obtain the contingency table and bar plot of the \texttt{pet} and
\texttt{vacation} data set.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

To obtain the contingency table and bar plot of the \texttt{pet} and
\texttt{vacation} data set, we use the \texttt{table()} and
\texttt{barplot()} functions.

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]

\end{tcolorbox}

\section{Behavioral survey from the Centers for Disease Control and
Prevention
(CDC)}\label{behavioral-survey-from-the-centers-for-disease-control-and-prevention-cdc}

The data set is slightly modified from
\href{https://www.openintro.org/book/statdata/?data=cdc}{OpenIntro},

\begin{quote}
The Behavioral Risk Factor Surveillance System (BRFSS) is an annual
telephone survey of 350,000 people in the United States collected by the
Centers for Disease Control and Prevention (CDC). As its name implies,
the BRFSS is designed to identify risk factors in the adult population
and report emerging health trends. For example, respondents are asked
about their diet and weekly physical activity, their HIV/AIDS status,
possible tobacco use, and even their level of healthcare coverage. The
\href{https://www.openintro.org/redirect.php?go=cdc_data_brfss&referrer=data_set_page}{BRFSS
Web site} contains a complete description of the survey, the questions
that were asked and even research results that have been derived from
the data.

This data set is a random sample of 20,000 people from the BRFSS survey
conducted in 2000. While there are over 200 questions or variables in
this dataset, this data set only includes 9 variables.
\end{quote}

The data set has the following variables:

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \texttt{genhlth} - General health, with categories Excellent, Very
  Good, Good, Fair, and Poor
\item
  \texttt{exerany} - Whether the respondent exercised in the past month
\item
  \texttt{hlthplan} - Whether respondent has some form of health
  coverage
\item
  \texttt{smoke100} - Whether respondent has smoked at least 100
  cigarettes in their entire life
\item
  \texttt{height} - Respondent's height in inches
\item
  \texttt{weight} - Respondent's weight in pounds
\item
  \texttt{wtdesire} - Respondent's desired weight in pounds
\item
  \texttt{age} - Respondent's age in years
\item
  \texttt{gender} - Respondent's gender
\end{itemize}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

Retrieve the first few respondents, a vector of variable names, and the
structure of the \texttt{cdc} data set.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

3      Good     Yes      Yes      Yes     60    105      105  49 Female
4      Good     Yes      Yes       No     66    132      124  42 Female

\end{verbatim}

\chapter{4B: Examining Numerical
Variables}\label{b-examining-numerical-variables}

\section{Data Sets}\label{data-sets-1}

\begin{Shaded}
\begin{Highlighting}[]
\FunctionTok{load}\NormalTok{(}\FunctionTok{url}\NormalTok{(}\StringTok{\textquotesingle{}https://github.com/hungtong/DS{-}01{-}101/raw/refs/heads/main/dataset/l4b\_data.rdata\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{))}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\section{Topics}\label{topics-7}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Basic variable types
\item
  Histogram
\item
  Mean and median
\item
  Quartiles and five-number summary
\item
  Interquartile range (IQR), variance, and standard deviation
\item
  Box plot
\item
  Scatter plot and correlation
\end{itemize}

\section{Basic Data Types}\label{basic-data-types}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  Recall that a variable can be \textbf{numerical} or
  \textbf{categorical}.
\end{itemize}

\includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/4_var_type.png}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  A \textbf{numerical variable} represents numbers that are meaningful
  to add, subtract, or take averages.
\item
  A \textbf{categorical variable} refers to specific categories that
  describe a characteristic.
\end{itemize}

\section{Histogram}\label{histogram}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  \textbf{Histogram} is like a \emph{bar plot} for numerical data, but
  there is no separation between the bars. Numbers are divided into bins
  and the frequency distribution of these bins is displayed.
\item
  From a histogram, we can learn about the data distribution

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \textbf{Shape:} Is it symmetric, left-skewed, or right-skewed? Is it
    unimodal or multimodal? How many peaks?
  \item
    \textbf{Typical Value:} Where do most data values seem to
    concentrate?
  \item
    \textbf{Spread:} What is the approximate range of the data? How far
    are data points from the typical value?
  \end{itemize}
\item
  In a \textbf{symmetric} distribution, the left tail approximately
  mirrors the right tail.
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/4_symmetric.png}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\tightlist
\item
  A data distribution is said to be \textbf{left-skewed} if its tail
  extends further to the left.

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Example:} age of retirement, lifetime.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  A distribution is said to be \textbf{right-skewed} if its tail extends
  further to the right.

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \emph{Example:} housing prices, salaries.
  \end{itemize}
\item
  Note that \textbf{skewness} is about the skinny tail
\end{itemize}

\begin{center}
\includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/4_skew.png}
\end{center}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Previous distributions with only one peak are called
  \textbf{unimodal}.
\item
  A distribution with exactly two peaks is called \textbf{bimodal}.

  \begin{center}
  \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/4_bimodal.png}
  \end{center}
\item
  When a distribution has more than one peak, it is called
  \textbf{multimodal}.

  \includegraphics{index_files/mediabag/4_multimodal.png}\{width=``397'',
  fig-align=``center''\}
\end{itemize}

\section{Histogram in R}\label{histogram-in-r}

\begin{itemize}
\item
  Histogram can be generated using the \texttt{hist()} function. The
  number of bins will be automatically determined by R, but we can also
  adjust by changing \texttt{breaks}.
\item
  Recall common graphical parameters in base R plotting:

  \begin{itemize}
  \tightlist
  \item
    \texttt{col} - add color to the plot
  \item
    \texttt{main} - main title label
  \item
    \texttt{xlab} - label for x-axis
  \item
    \texttt{ylab} - label for y-axis
  \item
    \texttt{xlim} - x-axis range
  \item
    \texttt{ylim} - y-axis range
  \item
    \texttt{cex.main} - size of main title
  \item
    \texttt{cex.lab} - size of axis labels
  \item
    \texttt{cex.axis} - size of tick labels
  \end{itemize}
\end{itemize}

💻 \textbf{Hands-On}

The \texttt{bus\_driver} data set was collected from bus drivers
employed by public corporations. Each data point gives the number of
traffic accidents in which each bus driver was involved during a 4-year
period. Obtain the histogram of this data set and comment on the data
distribution.

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]

The data distribution is right-skewed. A smaller number of accidents is
more common, which is a good thing.

\begin{Shaded}

\NormalTok{  bus\_driver,}

  \AttributeTok{col  =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}darkslategray3\textquotesingle{}}\NormalTok{,    }
  \AttributeTok{xlab =} \StringTok{\textquotesingle{}Accidents by Bus Drivers\textquotesingle{}}
\NormalTok{)}
\end{Highlighting}
\end{Shaded}

\includegraphics{ls4b_plotting_files/figure-pdf/unnamed-chunk-2-1.pdf}

\end{tcolorbox}

\begin{tcolorbox}[enhanced jigsaw, colbacktitle=quarto-callout-tip-color!10!white, bottomrule=.15mm, opacityback=0, title=\textcolor{quarto-callout-tip-color}{\faLightbulb}\hspace{0.5em}{Answer}, breakable, colframe=quarto-callout-tip-color-frame, opacitybacktitle=0.6, coltitle=black, bottomtitle=1mm, toptitle=1mm, titlerule=0mm, leftrule=.75mm, arc=.35mm, left=2mm, colback=white, rightrule=.15mm, toprule=.15mm]
